a\ngroup of young, like-minded entrepreneurs with a drive for success, upon\nbeing presented with a once in a life-time business opportunity. Our\nfirst business venture will be acquiring *Abraham Restaurant Industries,\nInc. (ARI),* leveraging an exclusive purchase agreement with a price\nsignificantly below market value, to drastically increase revenues and\nprofit margins by building from the progress made over the last three\nyears. The hospitality group currently consists of Le Bistro, a fine\ndining restaurant offering New American Cuisine with French flare, and\nThe Cellar Door, a tapas restaurant offering a variety of small plates\ninspired by classic Spanish tapas. Informally, ARI has a thriving\ncatering and special events business, with revenues pushing \\$200,000 a\nyear, and a furniture and fine arts retail business (Chairy Couture),\nwith modest yearly revenues with potential for significant growth.\nNavi's partners' immediate objective is to elevate the quality of\ncurrently offered products and services, improving guest retention and\nsatisfaction, with a commitment to proper staffing, extensive training,\nand functional systems and processes in day-to-day operations. Navi's\nongoing goals include providing excellence in all units of business,\nenhancing communities in which we operate, being an active partner to\nlocal non-profits, fostering employee growth, and creating opportunities\nfor employees to become entrepreneurs.\n\n- **Le Bistro** is a full service up-scale restaurant located in\n Downtown Huntington, WV, offering New American Cuisine for Lunch,\n Brunch, Dinner and Catering services. Le Bistro stands apart from\n competitors in the area with an atmosphere unfound anywhere else,\n including: fine art covering the walls (reminiscent of a \"big city'\n art gallery), an open kitchen, seasonal tasting menus, unique catering\n options, the highest quality ingredients (sustainable, no hormones, no\n antibiotics, free range, locally sourced when possible), and unique\n holiday events. Our goal is for every guest that dines with us to\n leave looking forward to their next visit, having had an unparalleled\n dining experience. Prior to re-opening our key objectives include\n front and back of house staff training, renovations that will improve\n efficiency and functionality throughout the kitchen and dining room,\n and adequate staffing for all restaurant positions.\n\n- **The Cellar Door** is a full-service restaurant and lounge featuring\n a tapas (small plates) concept located on the floor below Le Bistro.\n The Cellar Door is one of a kind; hand painted murals adorn the walls\n throughout the restaurant, with accent walls textured with ceiling\n medallions. Numerous styles of chandeliers are hung throughout the\n dining room, over the bar, and in the event room. Large lounge areas,\n designed for 6 to 12 people, are intermittently placed among regular\n dining tables, each made up of brightly colored, one of a kind\n refurbished chairs and couches (designed by owner, Pam Abraham),\n matching throw pillows, and large, custom wooden coffee tables. The\n food menu features a variety of small plates, meant to be shared with\n friends and enjoyed with one of the extensive offerings from the\n alcohol menu. Specialty cocktails, craft beer and bourbon are the\n focus of the alcohol menu, though the wine selection is well varied\n and features local West Virginia wines. As with Le Bistro, our goal is\n for every guest that dines with us to leave looking forward to their\n next visit, having had an unparalleled dining experience. Prior to\n re-opening our key objectives include front and back of house staff\n training, re-vamping menu options and presentation (food & specialty\n cocktails), and adequate staffing for all restaurant positions.\n\n**Mission Statement:** To approach every unique and diverse economic\nopportunity with entrepreneurial spirit, strategy, compassion, and\ncollective energy to facilitate company growth ultimately to benefit all\nstakeholders.\n\n**Company History:** Le Bistro opened in April 2012, under the ownership\nof Pam and Naz Abraham. Sales and guest retention grew steadily (20%+\nyear over year) from 2012 through December 2014. During that time Pam\nwas actively involved in restaurant operations, assisted by 3 managers\n(Robert Abraham, Matt Stickler, and Rob Crickard) and an executive chef\n(Brittany Barker). In 2015, Le Bistro's sister restaurant, The Cellar\nDoor, opened in the same building on the lower level. As a result of\ninternal conflict, inadequate staffing levels, inadequate training, and\nlack of consistency in concept and product during The Cellar Door's\nfirst year of operations, both restaurants saw significant decline in\nrevenues and guest count from the first quarter of 2015 through April\n2017. In April 2017, John Gladson was hired as executive chef, and\nshortly after, in May 2017, Chris Craven was hired as General Manager\nand Special Events Coordinator. Shortly after, Chris promoted Josh\nHalstead to Assistant Manager. By the end of 2017, the new management\nteam successfully reversed the decline in revenue and guest count. In\n2018, Chris hired Dakota Maddox as the Special Events Manager. Abraham\nRestaurant Industries saw continued growth, had the highest catering\nsales in restaurant history, and had a significant increase in\nprofitability (7%) as a result of successful efforts to reduce labor and\noperating costs. In 2019, management successfully implemented systems\nand processes related to inventory and recipe management, further\nincreasing profitability by reducing cost of goods sold. Le Bistro and\nThe Cellar Door have been closed since March 16^th^, 2020 due to the\nCOVID-19 pandemic. Pam and Naz Abraham decided this marked the right\ntime for retirement and offered General Manager and Special Events\nCoordinator, Chris Craven, the opportunity to purchase the business.\n\n**\\\nPast Performance:**\n\n**Gross Revenue 2013 -- 2019**\n\n![](media/image6.emf){width=\"6.844444444444444in\"\nheight=\"3.8554319772528434in\"}\n\n![](media/image7.emf){width=\"6.844444444444444in\"\nheight=\"3.8079013560804897in\"}**Cost of Goods Sold (COGS) 2013 -- 2019**\n\n![](media/image8.emf){width=\"7.0in\" height=\"3.670138888888889in\"}**Labor\nSummary 2013 -- 2019**\n\n![](media/image9.emf){width=\"7.0in\"\nheight=\"3.8847222222222224in\"}**Prime Cost Summary 2013 -- 2019**\n\n**April 2012 -- December 2014 (Growth):** Year-over-year growth by month\naveraged 10.3% during this time frame. The typical decline in sales as a\nresult of increased sales during the opening period lasted from June\n2013 through November 2013, with an average sales growth of -1.76%. The\n12-month average growth rate peaked January 2014 -- December 2014 with\nan average sales growth of 15.56%. The success in guest retention (thus\ngross revenue) during this period can be attributed to a better overall\nguest experience, resulting from a happy staff (culture) and more owner\nengagement. The positive business culture was directly tied to proper\nstaffing levels (during peak business days/times) and management\nsupport. While some of the management team had management experience\nduring this time, most did not have restaurant experience, resulting in\nhigh labor (improper staffing levels during slow days/times, and Owner\nSalary) and COGS expenses (no inventory management or recipe management,\nand minimal over-sight of kitchen employees), despite better business\nculture management. The graph below illustrates the trend in sales\ngrowth.\n\n**\\**\n\n**January 2015 -- April 2017 (Decline):** Year-over-year growth by month\naveraged -9.43% during this time frame. The decline in sales began one\nmonth after the opening of The Cellar Door, with an average sales growth\nof -9.86% from February 2015 -- January 2016. The 12-month average\ndecline in growth peaked in September 2016 at -20.30%. The graph below\nillustrates the trend in sales growth. The combination of inadequate\ntraining, understaffing and poor menu development led to a substantial\ndrop in the quality of service at both Le Bistro and The Cellar Door.\nThe lack of planning surrounding the opening of The Cellar Door\ndistracted from the success that was happening at Le Bistro, resulting\nin a negative impact on service, quality and efficiency in both\nlocations.\n\n**May 2017 -- February 2020 (Stabilization & Improved Profitability):**\nMay 1^st^, 2017, our current management team was hired, and we\nimmediately went to work on the most glaring issue: reversing revenue\nloss and guest retention decline. While it was clear this would be the\nfirst of many mountains to climb, this was our first focus, as prolonged\nsales decline is indicative of on-going negative guest experience and\nleft un-managed, could have resulted in permanent damage to our business\nreputation. We achieved an overall average monthly sales growth of\n4.85%, with substantial success in catering sales growth (10.04%) and\nCellar Door sales growth (22.56%); comparative to the previous overall\n12-month average sales decline of -15.92%, staggering Cellar Door sales\ndecline of -29.74% and stagnant catering sales (-0.34%).\n\nIn 2018, focus shifted to labor management and bringing labor levels to\nindustry standards. As a result, ARI saw the lowest labor cost percent\nin company history at 31.97%. Significant focus was also given to\nimprove communications throughout the leadership team, specifically\nregarding Catering and Event Inquiries. The initiative successfully led\nto further catering sales growth, with year-over monthly growth average\nreaching 24.65%. The graph below illustrates the labor trend from 2017\nthrough 2019.\n\nOur most recent focus, and final step in the three-year plan to\nprofitability, was in reducing cost of goods sold. The process began in\n2017, with implementation of monthly inventory counts, which lead to\nweekly inventory counts, exploration into inventory management software,\nrecipe management software, and new systems and processes throughout Le\nBistro & The Cellar Door. In 2019, we consulted with specialists from\nGordon Food Service, who helped implement the final stages of a complete\nrecipe and inventory management system. While the implementation and\ntraining process necessitated additional labor, our efforts lead to a 4%\n(\\$40,400) reductions in COGS, moving ARI into profitable margins for\nthe first time in 5 years.\n\nWhile we are proud of the successes that have been made, the highest\nlevels of efficiency and effectiveness were never fully realized due to\nthe owner's lack of industry knowledge, business experience, and\nperception of value in quality management.\n\n![](media/image10.emf){width=\"5.885714129483815in\"\nheight=\"4.133333333333334in\"}**Labor Summary 2017 -- 2019**\n\n![](media/image11.emf){width=\"5.885416666666667in\"\nheight=\"4.1339687226596675in\"}**Cost of Goods Sold Summary 2017 --\n2019**\n\n**Adjusted EDITDA 2017 -- 2019**\n\n![](media/image12.emf){width=\"6.508333333333334in\"\nheight=\"5.010416666666667in\"}\n\n**Services:**\n\nLe Bistro is a full-service restaurant operating in the fine dining\nsegment. Services include:\n\n- **Current**\n\n - Lunch Service (Monday -- Friday, 10:30 am -- 5:00 pm)\n\n - Dinner Service (Monday -- Thursday, 5:00 -- 9:00 pm \\| Friday &\n Saturday, 5:00 -- 10:00 pm)\n\n - Brunch Service (Saturday & Sunday, 10:00 am -- 4:00 pm)\n\n - Full-Service Bar (During all operating hours)\n\n - To Go & Delivery Services (During all operating hours)\n\n - Venue Buyout (During all operating hours plus additional times upon\n request)\n\n - *Catering\\**\n\n- **New**\n\n\n\n- Meal Kits (with delivery service)\n\n- Meal Planning\n\n- Wine & Beer Carry Out and Delivery\n\n- Art Consignment\n\n- Cooking Classes (Virtual & On-site)\n\n\n\n- **COVID-19**\n\n\n\n- Phase 1\n\n - Meal Kits with delivery option\n\n - Wine & Beer Carry Out and Delivery\n\n - Lunch To-Go Service (Limited Menu \\| Monday-Friday 11:00 am -- 3:00\n pm)\n\n - Dinner to Go Service (Limited Menu \\| Friday and Saturday 5:00 pm --\n 8:00 pm)\n\n - Catering to Go & Drop Off (During all operating hours)\n\n - Cooking Classes (Virtual)\n\n- Phase 2\n\n - Phase 1 Services\n\n - See current services at limited capacity\n\n- Phase 3\n\n - Phase 1 and 2 Services\n\n - Onsite catering services with limited capacity.\n\nCellar Door is a full service upscale, casual restaurant. Services\ninclude:\n\n- **Current**\n\n - Evening Service (Monday -- Thursday, 3:30 pm -- 10:00 pm \\| Friday &\n Saturday, 3:30 pm -- 12:00 am)\n\n - Full-Service Bar (During all operating hours)\n\n - Brunch Service (Saturday, 11:00 am -- 3:30 pm)\n\n - To Go & Delivery Services (During all operating hours)\n\n - Event Room Rental (During all operating hours plus additional times\n upon request)\n\n - Venue Buyout Option (During all operating hours plus additional\n times upon request)\n\n - *Catering\\**\n\n- **New**\n\n - Wine & Beer Carry Out and Delivery (During all operating hours plus\n additional times upon request)\n\n - Custom Furniture Retail (During all operating hours plus additional\n times upon request)\n\n- **COVID-19**\n\n\n\n- Phase 1\n\n - Wine & Beer Carry Out and Delivery (Orders taken Monday-Sunday with\n deliveries on Friday-Sunday)\n\n- Phase 2\n\n - Phase 1 Services\n\n - Full-service bar and dining with limited capacity (Monday --\n Thursday, 3:30 pm -- 10:00 pm \\| Friday & Saturday, 3:30 pm -- 12:00\n am)\n\n- Phase 3\n\n - Phase 1 and 2 Services\n\n - Event Room Rental with limited capacity (During all operating hours\n plus additional times upon request)\n\nCatering services offered by our team are of the utmost quality, with\nthe intention to provide each and every guest with an experience\ntailored to each of their wants and needs. This is accomplished through\nample time spent with guests to master their vision; offered menu items\nand services go beyond the standard. Services include:\n\n- **Current**\n\n - Pick Up: Brunch, Lunch, Dinner, and Hors d\\'oeuvres\n\n - Drop Off: Brunch, Lunch, Dinner, and Hors d\\'oeuvres\n\n - Real Display: Brunch, Lunch, Dinner, and Hors d\\'oeuvres\n\n - Full Service: Brunch, Lunch, Dinner, and Hors d\\'oeuvres\n\n- **New**\n\n - Event Planning and Coordinating Services\n\n - Event Staffing Services\n\n**Organizational Structure Overview:** Navi Inc. is a small business\ncorporation, or S Corp, headed by Chris Craven, Dakota Maddox, John\nGladson, and Josh Halstead. Chris Craven, BBA in Accounting and\nEconomics and M.Acct., is the founder and Chief Executive Officer. He\nhas just over a decade of experience in the restaurant industry where he\nhas successfully fulfilled multiple roles, including several years in\nmanagement over multiple restaurants including a fine dining restaurant\nand upscale casual tapas restaurant. For both restaurants, Chris was\nresponsible for most aspects of the organizations from marketing to\nstrategic planning. Dakota, MBA, is the Secretary and Chief Experience\nOfficer. She has ten years of experience in the industry wearing\nmultiple hats for all front of house positions. Dakota has been\nprimarily responsible for coordinating and planning special events,\nmarketing initiatives, and creating internal systems and processes to\nimprove efficiency. John Gladson attended the most prestigious culinary\nschool in the states, the Culinary Institute of America (CIA). He is the\nExecutive Vice President and Chief Operating Officer who also has ten\nyears of experience in the restaurant industry. John has 10 years of\nculinary experience from a multitude of concepts, 8 years of restaurant\nmanagement experience, and 1 year of brewery experience in a\nmicrobrewery. John has been classically trained and specializes in\nFrench cuisine and techniques. Josh Halstead, BBA in Management, is Navi\nInc.'s Chief Human Resources Officer. He has nine years of restaurant\nexperience, 3 years of management and hiring experience, and 3 years of\ntraining, policy, and procedure development experience. Josh specializes\nin customer relations, employee development and retention.\n\n**Organizational Structure: *\\*****As per the Articles of Incorporation\nand Bylaws of Navi Inc.*\n\n- **Chris Craven -- Chief Executive Officer (CEO):** The Chief Executive\n Officer shall be the President of the Corporation, responsible for the\n ultimate oversight of the Corporation\\'s actions. The CEO shall\n preside at Shareholder meetings, track and supervise that Board\n resolutions are carried out, and sign Corporate documents. Subject to\n the control and supervisory powers of the Board and its delegate, the\n powers and duties of the CEO will be: \n\n\n\n- To have the general management and supervision, direction and control\n of the business and affairs of the Corporation; \n\n- To preside at all meetings of the Shareholders and at meetings of the\n Board when the Chairman of the Board is absent; \n\n- To call meetings of the Shareholders to be held at such times and as\n such places as the Chief Executive Officer will deem proper within the\n limitations prescribed by law or by these bylaws; \n\n- To ensure that all orders and resolutions of the Board are effectively\n carried out; \n\n- To maintain records of and certify, whenever necessary, all\n proceedings of the Board and the Shareholders; \n\n- To put the signature of the Corporation to all deeds, conveyances,\n mortgages, guarantees, leases, obligations, bonds, certificates and\n other papers and instruments in writing which have been authorized by\n the Board or which, in the opinion of the Chief Executive Officer,\n should be executed on behalf of the corporation; to sign certificates\n for the Corporation's shares; and, subject to the instructions of the\n Board, to have general charge of the property of the Corporation and\n to supervise and manage all Officers, agents and employees of the\n Corporation; and \n\n- To perform all other duties and carry out other responsibilities as\n determined by the Board. \n\n\n\n- **Qualifications**\n\n - *BBA in Accounting*\n\n - *BBA in Economics*\n\n - *M.Acct. from Marshall University*\n\n - *11 years of restaurant experience*\n\n - 3 years of General Management experience\n\n - 2 years as lead server with ARI\n\n - 6 months of service professional training with Darden Restaurants\n\n\n\n- **John Gladson -- Chief Operating Officer (COO):** The Chief Operating\n Officer shall be the Executive Vice President of the Corporation. If\n the President is not available or dies, is incapacitated or refuses to\n act, the Executive Vice President will perform the duties of the\n President, and when so acting, the Executive Vice President will be\n subject to the same powers and limitations of the President; and the\n Executive Vice President will perform any other duties as from time to\n time may be delegated to the Executive Vice President by the President\n or the Board. \n\n\n\n- To have general management and supervision, direction and control over\n the day to day business dealings of the Corporation;\n\n- The design, operation, and improvement of the systems that create and\n deliver the firm's products and services; \n\n- To ensure compliance with the Corporation's policies and procedures; \n\n- To manage business relationships with key suppliers and ensure that\n the Corporation's products and services meet standards of quality and\n cost effectiveness; \n\n- To develop and implement space-planning strategies to accommodate\n current and future organizational needs; \n\n- To coordinate staff for coverage in all related areas of\n the departments; \n\n- To assist in attaining the Corporation's established operational and\n financial goals; and \n\n- To perform all other duties and carry out other responsibilities as\n prescribed by the Board or the Chief Executive Officer. \n\n\n\n- **Qualifications**\n\n - *Attended the Culinary Institute of America*\n\n - *10 years of restaurant experience*\n\n - *8 years of restaurant management experience*\n\n - 3 years of management experience with ARI\n\n\n\n- **Benjamin Halstead -- Chief Human Resources Officer\n (CHRO): **The Chief Human Resources Officer shall be responsible for\n all aspects of human resource management and industrial relations\n policies, practices and operations for the restaurants; with ultimate\n oversight of cultivating creative leaders, mobilizing for greater\n speed and flexibility in talent allocation, and capitalizing on\n collective intelligence through effective collaboration.\n\n\n\n- To build quality and depth of talent, including a focus on succession\n and leadership/employee development; \n\n- To manage corporate capabilities dealing with changes in technology,\n government regulation and public policy; \n\n- To manage external context, including external stakeholders, local and\n national environment, as well as key drivers and important trends that\n influence the Corporation's objectives. To include stakeholder values,\n perceptions, and relationships, as well as the Corporation's social,\n cultural, political, legal, regulatory, technological, economic,\n natural, and competitive environment; \n\n- To ensure effective operations by managing a multi-generational\n workforce, adapting to change, and operating effectively in different\n business structures; \n\n- To provide leadership in helping shape the culture of the company,\n ensuring that the values of the company are communicated and\n understood at all levels, providing clarity as to the expected\n behavior of all employees and the development of a high-performance\n culture; \n\n- To establish and maintain high levels of employee engagement\n and commitment; \n\n- To ensure situations in which employee behavior is inconsistent with\n the values of the Corporation are dealt with fairly; \n\n- To establish a culture that is supportive of external partnerships, as\n sources of innovation, capabilities and growth. \n\n- To perform all other duties and carry out other responsibilities as\n prescribed by the Board or the Chief Executive Officer.\n\n\n\n- **Qualifications**\n\n responsibilities as\n prescribed by the Board or the Chief Executive Officer.\n\n\n\n- **Qualifications**\n\n\n\n- *MBA with a Concentration in Marketing from Marshall University*\n\n- *10 years of team*\n\n![](media/image13.png){width=\"10.69811132983377in\" height=\"5.90625in\"}\n\n**Financing Goals:**\n\n![](media/image14.emf){width=\"6.958333333333333in\"\nheight=\"5.333333333333333in\"}\n\n# Business Description\n\n**Opportunity:**\n\n- Growing market which will continue to increase due to the large focus\n on the community revitalization projects for downtown Huntington\n\n - Medical Hub\n\n - Fairfield Browns\n\n - Hotel Renovations\n\n - University Expansion\n\n - \n\n- Strategic local alliances offering sources of referrals and joint\n marketing ventures to extend the reach of the restaurants\n\n - \n\n \n\n - My Huntington\n\n - Huntington Pride\n\n - Huntington Downtown Partners\n\n - Boutiques on the Avenues\n\n - Create Huntington\n\n - Marshall University\n\n - \n\n- Key location in downtown, across from a high-trafficked retail and\n entertainment are, Pullman Square\n\n- Both restaurants offering a unique atmosphere and experience unlike\n any in the tri-state metropolitan area\n\n- Limited competition in the fine dining sector (1 competitor in\n downtown Huntington, 2 competitors in a 10-mile radius, 3 competitors\n in a 20-mile radius)\n\n- Event planning and catering underserved in local and surrounding area\n\n- Increase and develop a number of preferred vendor relationships with\n florists, photographers, bakers, event planners, venues,\n videographers, DJs, and live musicians\n\n- Braidy Industries opened headquarters in Ashland area and is building\n a revolutionary aluminum manufacturing plant. This will result in over\n 4000 jobs and will bring \\$1.54 billion to Eastern Kentucky by the end\n of 2021. There will be an increased opportunity for caterings as well\n as new entrants to the fine dining market\n\n- Offering unique opportunity to view and purchase fine, local art and\n custom, eccentric furniture\n\n - Le Bistro's dining space currently acts as an art gallery that will\n eventually double as consigning wall space for local artists\n\n - Cellar Door is an interactive showroom for Chairy Couture and all of\n the current custom furnishing offerings\n\n- No other local meal kit/meal prep provider\n\n - Meal Kit industry to grow 25 to 30% by 2022\n\n - 49% of consumers say they would buy meal kits from their favorite\n restaurants\n\n - With the meal kit industry growing so rapidly it is important for\n restaurants to tap into the market\n\n - Due to COVID-19 sales for meal kits and home delivery have increased\n dramatically\n\n- Beer and Wine now legal to be delivered\n\n - Alcohol carry out and delivery sales have become essential to\n revenue streams for restaurants during COVID-19\n\n - With 20 to 30 percent of sales for restaurants being alcohol the\n legalization of carry out and delivery has become vital for business\n\n - The 2020 Liquor License Renewal includes the addition of beer and\n wine delivery, indicating this policy will remain in place post\n COVID-19\n\n- Support for young entrepreneurs in Huntington\n\n - Huntingtonians working to improve the Huntington area know it is\n vital for the city to retain young professionals. We have the\n opportunity to use our collective knowledge to create the best\n dining experience in Huntington, with avid support from our target\n demographic, as those working to improve Huntington are those with\n the means to do so.\n\n- COVID-19: Summary of opportunity created\n\n - 2020 Employee Retention Tax Credit\n\n - Projections for tax credit to be extended through 2021\n\n - National Restaurant Association lobbying for Federal Grant Program\n Reimbursing Restaurants for lost sales due to COVID-19 for the 2019\n calendar year\n\n - The tax deduction for business meals and entertainment is to be\n restored in 2021, specifically benefitting the up-scale casual and\n fine dining segments by incentivizing business professionals\n\n - Numerous large corporations have started grant programs offering\n financial assistance to small, privately owned restaurants\n\n - State income tax relief. The filing and payment date for WV state\n income taxes is extended from April 15 to July 15, 2020. This also\n applies to estimated tax payments for tax year 2020 that are due\n between April 15 and July 15, 2020. \n\n - Landlord has agreed to waive rent from the time of acquisition until\n 2 months after the restaurant dining rooms re-open for dine-in\n service and is providing a 50% discount for the following two\n months. Additionally, he will be splitting the cost of floor\n renovations for the Le Bistro kitchens\n\n - Beer & Wine Delivery has been legalized in the state of West\n Virginia for Restaurants, providing a new revenue steam\n\n - The Alcohol Beverage Control Administration (ABC) has created a new\n (no charge) stream-lined process for an outdoor dining application\n to allow restaurants to register and serve beer, wine and liquor in\n the space\n\n - The City of Huntington has expedited the application process for\n outdoor dining\n\n**Product Overview:** High quality products with a focus on innovation,\nsustainability, and green practices.\n\n- **Le Bistro**\n\n - **Lunch Food -** Fast and efficient service with a focus on soup,\n salad, and sandwiches\n\n - Pairing down and updating previous menus to streamline efficiency\n\n - 34+ items will be reduced to approximately 20\n\n - Efforts to reduce menu size will result in faster ticket times a\n projected difference of 15 minutes to 8 minutes\n\n - A more concentrated effort on a fewer number of items to improve\n quality and profitability by reducing loss related to food waste\n and prep labor\n\n - Less time spent preparing items will allow cooks more time to\n give proper attention to every item on the menu\n\n - There will be less waste due to product loss that is not being\n sold or turned over fast enough\n\n - **Dinner Food -** High end dishes created with classical French\n technique\n\n - Pairing down and updating previous menus to reflect a more modern\n approach to dishes\n\n - 25+ items will be reduced to approximately 20\n\n - Efforts to reduce menus size will result in faster ticket times\n a projected difference of 20-25 minutes to 12-15 minutes\n\n - Taking a slightly more modern approach to dishes will set ARI\n apart from local competitors and create a more unique experience\n for guests\n\n - Menu creation will focus on composed dishes, with special\n attention to elements outside of the main protein, resulting\n in harmonious, comprehensive flavor combinations\n\n - A continued effort to give attention to sustainable products\n\n - Sustainable practices for food products are not only an\n incredible marketing tool, but it is also reflected in the\n flavors on the plate\n\n - **Meal Kits -** Quality ingredients packaged and delivered with\n expert cooking instructions\n\n - During Covid-19 and beyond meal kits will be an easy way to\n increase revenue by providing easy access to high-end ingredients\n not available to the public at large\n\n - **Wine -** Attention to Old World wines and top tier New World wines\n\n - Wine menu will be more reflective of popular items and current\n industry trends\n\n - More care will be given to making sure menus reflect current\n inventory to prevent customer dissatisfaction\n\n - With the use of Upserve these numbers will be easy to track and\n take action on\n\n - **Beer -** Variety of choices with regional and small breweries\n being priority\n\n - Beer pairings suggestions for dishes will be part of server\n training\n\n - Beer menu will be more reflective of popular items and current\n industry trends\n\n - **Spirits -** Premium selection of spirits served in interesting and\n unique ways\n\n - Small, seasonal cocktail menus will provide bartenders the\n opportunity to showcase premium liquors\n\n - Implementation of new techniques and serving styles will elevate\n the guest experience through innovative and interactive\n presentation\n\n - **Art -** Art consignment with local artists and small art\n exhibitions as the focal point\n\n - Paintings will now have small signage next to them denoting artist\n and pricing\n\n - A more concerted effort will be made by servers to talk about the\n art with customers, facilitated through new training procedures\n\n - As current collection of paintings are sold they will be replaced\n with art by local artists to be consigned, providing another\n avenue for community engagement\n\n- **The Cellar Door**\n\n - **Food -** Small plates and sharable dishes\n\n - A shift away from the term \"tapas\" will allow for a more creative\n menu that does not restrict itself to traditional Spanish fare\n\n - Since open The Cellar Door has never been able to execute tapas\n as a concept properly\n\n - With many guests being confused or unclear about the concept a\n shift towards small plates will make it easier to understand and\n market\n\n - Properly sizing small items will allow for customers to order a\n variety of dishes giving servers more opportunity to up sell\n\n - **Wine -** Attention to New World wines and unconventional\n varieties, with flights available\n\n - Wine menu will be more reflective of popular items and industry\n trends\n\n - A stronger emphasis on using wine in mixed drinks such as sangria,\n punches, etc. will add variety to the menu while reducing wine\n waste\n\n - **Beer -** Variety of choices with regional and small breweries\n being the priority, with flights available\n\n - Many regional breweries have taken large steps to produce quality\n products over the past years and have begun to grow a following\n\n - Highlighting these local and regional beers has, and will continue\n to draw in more guests\n\n - Focusing on local product further reduces our carbon footprint\n\n - **Spirits -** Vast array of spirits with a focus on flights,\n bourbon, and distinctive cocktails\n\n - Small, seasonal cocktail menus will provide bartenders the\n opportunity to showcase premium liquors\n\n - Implementation of new techniques and serving styles will elevate\n the guest experience\n\n - Increased availability of local spirits has resulted in recent\n growth of popularity, allowing the introduction and focus on these\n products\n\n- **Catering**\n\n - **On-site -** Utilizing the event room as well as the Touma Museum\n to serve up to 200 guests.\n\n - **Off-site -** Staffing, servicing, and delivering food for events\n both large and small in any location our licensing permits.\n\n - **Food -** Completely tailored menu and service styles to meet all\n guest needs, with specialty in Weddings, Corporate, and Social\n Events.\n\n - Catering menus have been designed to offer guests a range of\n options to work with any occasion while working with products\n already in use at the restaurants\n\n - Providing guests with a large amount of control over their\n ordering allows ARI to fill any needs in a market where catering\n services are scarce\n\n- **Alcohol --** Alcoholic selections are completely customizable based\n on guests' preferences, needs, and budget. Local and regional entities\n will remain a focus as well as any sort of specials possible based on\n available inventory.\n\n- **Catering Equipment and Supplies** -- A substantial collection of\n cooking and holding supplies and equipment, beverage dispensers and\n beverageware, displays, stands, and décor, and tabletop supplies\n including dinnerware, flatware, linens and table covers, and cloth\n napkins create opportunity for guest savings on rental fees from\n outside vendors and additional revenue with minimal rental fees added\n to our supplies.\n\n**Key Participants:**\n\n- **Current --** Upserve, GFS, Buzz Food Service, Capital Beverages,\n Mountain State Beverage, Spriggs Distributing, North Central\n Distributors, Atomic Beverages, King's Spirits, Stadium Spirits,\n Classic Liquors, The Keith Albee, Marshall University, A to Z Rentals\n\n- **Potential --** Event Planners: Be Merry and Alyssa B. Events,\n Florists: Archer's, Spurlock's, Three Birds Floral, Garrisons Designs,\n Hotels: Delta Hotel by Marriott, DoubleTree by Hilton, Venues: Keith\n Albee, Little Tennessee Event Farm, Venue on Madison, Camayo Room,\n Paramount Arts Center, Marshall University Foundation, Annie Lane,\n Parks Board (Ritter Park Amphitheater and Harris Riverfront), Twin\n Creeks Farms, Photographers: Mark Webb Photography, Vince Alonzo\n Photo, Michael Cole, Monica Thorne, Tonya Rayburn Dolin, Josh Stapler,\n Michael L Farmer, Ashley Arthur, Amanda Brewer, Lavender Photography,\n Ethan Witt, Stacey Parsley, Sammi Lawson, Autumn Vallandingham,\n Natasha Raichel, Courtney Quinn Christian, Natasha Baker, WE\n Photography, Brittany Bellomy, Alondra Wilcoxon Photography, Paula\n Vega Cakes, Nomada, Sweet Street, Sweet & Sassy, Videographer:\n Bakeries: DJs/Live Entertainment: DJ Bravo, Luminary DJ Company, DJ\n illSpin,\n\n![](media/image15.emf){width=\"4.113888888888889in\"\nheight=\"7.738194444444445in\"}**Pricing:** Pricing strategies for all\nmenus will be based around increasing profitability, increasing revenue\nper customer, and staying competitive within the current market. Price\npoints for all locations and meal periods will stay in the same range\nwithin a few dollars of current pricing (see below). It will be\nimportant to keep pricing in a range that has high perception of value\nto guests while maintaining profitability.\n\n**Le Bistro**\n\n**Cellar Door**\n\n**Catering**\n\n# Market Analysis\n\n**Industry Type:** Hospitality (Food and Beverage) - ARI provides a\nrange of options for satisfying customers. From two full-service\nrestaurants, to on and off-site catering, ARI fills many needs within\nthe community.\n\n**Summary:** Huntington is a city located in the two most western\ncounties, Cabell and Wayne, of West Virginia. It is a historic and\nbustling city of commerce and heavy industry, benefiting from its\nlocation on the Ohio River. The city is surrounded by regions that offer\nextensive natural resources such as coal, oil, chemicals and steel that\nsupport the local economy. In the last decade, several local initiatives\nto restore and grow the downtown area thus creating more diverse support\nfor the economy; with focus on locally owned shops and restaurants, the\nart community, and area parks and green spaces.\n\nAccording to the US Census Bureau quick facts, Huntington is a medium\nsized town with a population of approximately 46,048. Looking outside of\ncity limits and expanding to 10-mile radius, the population increases to\nnearly 78,000 people. Additionally, Huntington is located in West\nVirginia's largest metropolitan population of 365,419. There were\napproximately 19,755 households in 2019 with a median household income\nof \\$30,362. The residential population in the immediate area is\ncomprised of a mixture of single family and multi-family housing. The\nquick facts indicate that the population in Huntington, WV for those\nunder 5 years old is 6.0%; under 18 years old is 18.5%; between 18 and\n65 years of age is 60.2; and over 65 years old is 15.3%. Of which 85.4%\nare White alone; 8.7% are Black of African American alone; 3.0% are Two\nor More Races; 2.0% are Hispanic or Latino; 1.6% are Asian; .3% are\nAmerican Indian and Alaska native; .1% are Native Hawaiian and Other\nPacific Islander alone. Lastly, 51.1% are female and conversely 48.9%\nare male; with 6.2% of the total population are veterans.\n\nHuntingtonians are influenced by Appalachian Culture, Southern culture,\nMidwestern culture, and Mid-Atlantic Culture.\n\nMajor employment segments in Huntington, WV are trade, transportation\nand utilities, government, educational and health services, business and\nprofessional services, leisure and hospitality, and manufacturing. The\nlargest employers in the area include Marshall University,\nCabell-Huntington Hospital, St. Mary's Medical Center, Amazon, U.S.\nCorps of Engineers, Cabell Co. Board of Education, CSX Huntington, VA\nMedical Center, Braidy Industries, and the City of Huntington.\n\n**Segmentation:** ARI will appeal to a broad base of consumers in both\nthe residential and business community; people that have a desire for\nexceptional food, quality service, and a fascinating atmosphere. The\nlocation, of the two restaurants housed under ARI, was chosen primarily\nto appeal to the growing number of professionals living and working in\ndowntown Huntington. In looking at the market analysis, we have defined\nthe following groups as our targeted markets.\n\n> ***Professionals***: Business consumers need a competent establishment\n> that impresses their clients and prospects and creates an environment\n> for networking. The professionals in our area are impressed with our\n> quick service lunches and up-scale dinner experiences, sophisticated\n> atmospheres, and choice of private and semi-private dining spaces.\n>\n> ***Couples***: Dining out for a special occasion, regular date night,\n> or just an evening out with friends without the children. Le Bistro\n> and Cellar Door wow couples with our intimate and romantic setting,\n> quality service and ever-changing menu offerings, and special and\n> holiday promotions.\n>\n> ***Socializers***: View dining out as entertainment and an opportunity\n> to interact with peers. This group of people remain in awe of our\n> unique and eclectic settings, diverse food items, extensive beverage\n> selection, tasting evenings, and special events.\n>\n> ***Out of Towners***: Mostly traveling for business and dining alone,\n> these consumers look for a unique experience to the town their working\n> in while also staying close to their hotel. We initially attract them\n> with our convenient locations, trendy menu, wine tasting evenings and\n> special events, striking artwork gallery; we guarantee them as a\n> return visit with our excellent service and engaging clientele that\n> will be an entertaining and intellectually captivating experience by\n> itself.\n>\n> ***Business and Social Catering Customers***: Business catering\n> customers include office managers and administrators, event planners,\n> HR/training coordinators, and medical sales professionals. These\n> consumers place frequent orders with minimal notice for weekday\n> business events, such as meetings, training sessions and company\n> events. These consumers seek hassle free ordering from a menu\n> selection that includes box lunches, platters, buffet-style, and\n> \"build your own\" options, efficient pick up or drop off systems, and\n> convenient billing and payment processes. Social catering customers\n> are individuals who place orders for family gatherings, special\n> occasions, weddings and other functions. These consumers place orders\n> more infrequently, but there are a larger number of them. They\n> generally prefer to give advanced notice to ensure their vision and\n> needs are met within their budget. These consumers appreciate our\n> tailored menus that adhere to most social gathering needs and fit with\n> most budgets, our vast collection of catering supplies and décor, our\n> on-site event spaces, and our full range of catering services offered\n> on and off-site.\n\n**\\**\n\n**Key The options for people in the area are extremely\nlimited and do not come close to the quality and care of service ARI\nprovides. With on and off-site options available, in addition to, an\nextensive catering menu, ARI can fill almost any guest's needs.\n\nLe Bistro sets itself apart from its local competitors by offering a\nmodern take on classic food offerings, making a concerted effort in\ncreating a distinctive and enjoyable experience, and having a higher\nstandard of quality in every aspect of service.\n\nThe Cellar Door offers a vibrant and eclectic atmosphere unique to the\narea as the only \"small plates\" restaurant within 45 miles. It\ndifferentiates itself by focusing on group gatherings, shareable items,\nand an extensive alcohol selection; all within a one of a kind space\nfeaturing custom furniture, beautiful dining lounges, and a private\nevent room.\n\n**Current Positioning:** ARI positions itself as the premier fine dining\nand upscale-casual restaurant options in the Huntington and surrounding\narea. We have established this by providing excellent food and drink\nitems, prepared with quality ingredients at competitive rates. Guests\nenjoy the elegant and eccentric surroundings inside with the fine art\ndisplayed on the walls, custom furniture to relax on, and intentional\nambient lighting.\n\nOur guests enjoy our standard menu fare, along with seasonal and special\nevent menus, allowing us to better take advantage of cost savings and\nstay current with food industry trends.\n\n+------------------------+:-------------------------:+----------------------+\n| STRENGTHS | | WEAKNESSES |\n| | | |\n| - To capitalize on\nthis, continued improvements to the store front will make both locations\nmore visible to passers-by.\n\n**Uniqueness --** The Cellar Door and Le Bistro present guests with a\ndistinctive atmosphere that is unlike anything else seen in Huntington.\nMore emphasis will be put on using this as a marketing tool by taking\nmore photos and videos of the spaces**.**\n\n**Local Alliances --** Members of the ownership team have made many\nconnections within Huntington over the years. These connections will\noffer sources of referrals, join marketing, shared services, and greater\npresence in the market. Continued work within the community will grow\nthese relationships, as well as, forge new ones.\n\n**Key Employees --** Key Employees with decades of experience in the\nrestaurant industry and strong relationships with members of the\ncommunity\n\n**Quality Facilities --** Both Le Bistro and Cellar Door are\nfully-equipped with high-end equipment, tableware, fixtures, furniture\nand décor that is immediately evident upon entering.\n\n**Established Reputation --** Since the inception of Le Bistro it has\nbeen highly regarded in the area. The management staff worked tirelessly\nover the last few years to continue to improve this perception. The\nstaff has successfully held special events, offered extravagant dinners\non holidays and served beautiful weddings over the last few years. These\nefforts have made Le Bistro and The Cellar Door very well-known and\nsought-after locations. This will prove quite advantageous with the\nrelaunch of the restaurants. The already established reputation will\nhelp the management staff to hit the ground running and continue to grow\nexponentially.\n\n**Trend Setting/Adaptable --** The young management staff is constantly\ntrying to learn and adapt to the latest in restaurant trends. Too often\npeople who have found success in something will continue to do what they\nknow works without ever trying to adapt and change. The team will keep\nour operations fluid and search out any way to give ourselves a\ncompetitive advantage or put our restaurants ahead of the curve.\n\n**Experience of Leadership --** All of the management staff have been in\npositions of leadership for quite some time. Though the management team\nis young, they have nearly 15 years of management experience combined.\nThe entire team have had a higher form of education as well as\nexperience pertinent to the restaurant industry. The combination of\nyouth and experience will lead to even more growth in a management team\nthat has already found success.\n\n**Goods and Services Offered --** ARI made a commitment to give guests\nthe pleasure of \"Experiencing the Flavor of Quality.\" The way we seek to\ndo this is by purchasing ingredients of the highest quality. The\ncommitment to free-range, farm-centric, no hormone and sustainability\nallows us to really stand apart from what any competitor is doing in the\narea. We also have unique offerings to our area like our Bloody Mary\nBar.\n\n**Customer List/Customer Following --** Through the time both ARI\nlocations have been open they have been collecting data on the customers\nthat come in the door. This has resulted in a robust amount of customer\ndata for the management team to use when making decisions about\nstrategy. We have also implemented technology to allow us to email every\ncustomer on our email list. We can use this to communicate specials or\nsend out coupons.\n\n**Weaknesses**\n\n**Unorganized --** The lack of there always being proper management\nworking lead to disorganization. Often, tasks were forgotten or put off\nbecause there were too few people trying to do too many jobs. Moving\nforward we will combat this by utilizing an Executive Assistant to keep\neveryone on track. There will also be much more regimentation as to what\nresponsibilities will belong to who. These changes should help mitigate\nany issues with organization\n\n**Inconsistent Product --** Proper training and oversight of daily\nprocesses will combat any pervious issues of inconsistency. Initial\ntraining before we reopen will be quite intensive for both Front of\nHouse and Back of House positions. The new POS system, Upserve, will\nalso greatly aid in this endeavor. The chefs will be fully utilizing the\ninventory tracking capabilities to easily be able to tell if product is\nbeing mis proportioned.\n\n**Staff Training/Knowledge --** The initial training of all staff before\nreopening will be over two weeks of time that will go very in depth on\neverything from menu to processes. The CHRO will be revisiting the\ntraining process as well as heavily updating it. With so little\nmanagement time to be put into this, it was not able to be done\nconsistently. There will be a much larger management team to ensure that\ntraining is consistent and thorough every time.\n\n**Access to Additional Capital --** Lack of Capital -- Extensive\nplanning has gone into procurement of funds to begin business and\nprocedures have been put into place to prevent previous mistakes made by\npast ownership and management. Access to additional operating capital is\nan area that we are all actively seeking out to provide a safety net for\nARI.\n\n**Curb Appeal/Storefront Visibility --** The Cellar Door is located in a\nbasement and is hard to draw a guest's\n\neyes to. To remedy this, we will be placing a tv above the entrance. We\nhope this will help to attract the attention of people walking by. This\ntv will be used to educate people on our menu as well as guide them down\nthe stairs.\n\n**Decentralized Kitchen Management --** Le Bistro and The Cellar Door\nhave both operated without an executive chef for some time now. Le\nBistro had recently hired a new executive chef and the role was\nbeginning to be defined. Moving forward the roles of the leaders in the\nkitchen will be much more defined. The COO will personally take a hand\nin the kitchen management with the Executive Chef and Kitchen Manager\nbeing there to support him and insure proper implementation.\n\n**First Movers in Local Restaurant Scene --** Part of what makes this\nmanagement team great can also hurt us in some respects. While we try to\nalways stay ahead of the curve, we can occasionally be too far ahead.\nKnowing your market is important and there are many trends that are not\nin Huntington, WV yet. Our time trying out these new trends has led us\nto a better understanding of what is best for the consumers in our area.\n\n**Opportunities**\n\n**Innovation --** Technology and innovation are very important to ARI.\nWe try to always seek out better and more efficient ways of doing tasks\nin our restaurants. One way we will be innovating moving forward will be\nthe use of table side tablets. These tablets will increase efficiency as\nwell as offer touchless options for our guests. We believe that these\ntouchless options will really help to set us apart, especially in a post\nCOVID-19 world.\n\n**Area Growth --** Huntington has begun a revitalization project that\nhas and will bring in more businesses and increased tourism, expansion\nand further development of Marshall University.\n\n**New Ownership --** ARI will see a significate increase in guest\nnumbers upon reopen because of new ownership. A marketing campaign based\naround new ownership will only elevate these numbers.\n\n**Press/Media Coverage --** There is always an opportunity for free\npress when starting or buying a business. We will utilize this as much\nas possible in our early days. Anything from interviews to press\nreleases will help us get the message of our brand to new customers and\ndo so for free.\n\n**Government Aid/Support --** There will be many forms of aid available\nto ARI. The government has already move forward with a tax relief act\nthat will save us more than \\$80,000 in 202 alone. The management team\nwill be actively pursuing any other avenues of aid that are presented.\n\n**Increase in Labor Market --** COVID-19 has displaced many industry\nworkers. ARI will capitalize on this by holding extensive interviews\nwith as many candidates as possible to find the best employees that fit\nour needs. The flood of workers back to the market will help us staff\nboth locations with experienced workers.\n\n**Increased Local Alliances --** Towards the end of 2019 a massive\neffort was put forth to collaborate with local groups. Moving forward we\nwill continue to grow and foster these relationships. The name ARI will\nbecome synonymous with many different local organizations that are\naligned with our values.\n\n**To-Go/Drop-Off/Carry Out --** These more casual caterings are\nsomething that have not been heavily focused on in the past. The numbers\nfor these areas will grow with a catering coordinator seeking out new\ncustomers and keeping up with it. There will also be a designated To-Go\nperson during the day as well as hosts during the evenings.\n\n**Underserved Catering Market --** The catering market in the area has\nbeen underserved for quite some time. The CXO will work with our\ncatering coordinator to expand our share of the market. There has been\nmuch growth in this area since the beginning of the current management\nstaff's tenure. This is an area it is hard to predict because the growth\nof caterings could be exponential. The goal is to lead to a full-service\ncatering business that takes care of everything from the planning to the\nfood.\n\n**Lack of Competition (Le Bistro) --** There are only 3 other\nrestaurants within twenty miles that are considered competition for Le\nBistro. In the time Le Bistro has been open there have been several\n\"fine-dining\" places to close. The fact that Le Bistro has found success\nwhile so many other places have not, bodes well for us moving forward.\nLe Bistro is still the newest of any of its competitors and will look to\naggressively take customers from the limited competition it has.\n\n**Preferred Vendor Relationships --** the CXO will be heavily working\nwith vendors in the area to establish a relationship with them. It is\nthe goal of the management staff to get information on our services in\nany place that may be relevant.\n\n**Ongoing Focus to Support Local --** Supporting local is something that\nhas been more and more important to consumers every year. This has been\na task that the management team worked hard to do whenever applicable.\nThe COO will be in charge on ensuring we have an even broader array of\nlocal products than we had before. We will further expand on this by\nallowing local artists to display their art in our dining room.\n\n**10-Year Industry Growth Projection --** Even with the impact of\nCOVID-19 the restaurant industry is still projected to grow. Younger\nconsumers have decided that they care more about experiences than\nthings. Restaurants benefit from this fact greatly. As younger people\ncontinue to eat up more buying power in the market, restaurants will\ncontinue to grow.\n\n**Legalized Beer and Wine Delivery in State --** Due to COVID-19 it has\nbecome legal in the state to deliver wine and beer in WV. This is a\ngreat opportunity for us to expand into a different type of market. ARI\nhas access to many wines and beers that cannot be found in grocery\nstores. Implementing some sort or delivery service would not cost much\nat all and would help us to establish even greater revenue.\n\n**Threats**\n\n**New Event Venues --** Several new event locations have been built in\nthe area recently. This is good for our catering business. The issue\narises in that some of them have kitchens or catering contracts out to\nother companies. It will be important for us to try and reach out to\nthese locations in the hopes of making a deal with them. One major\nlocation we have been working on a deal with is the Marshall Alumni\nCenter. We hope to be able to serve anywhere in the area.\n\n**Customer Perception --** Anytime there is young leadership there will\nbe questions as to their expertise. It will be up to the management team\nto dissuade this feeling in any of our guests. We hope to surprise\neveryone with how thorough and knowledgeable we are. We also hope to aid\nin the fight against the perception that youth makes you less capable.\n\n**Economic Environment --** The economic environment coming out of\nCOVID-19 is still uncertain to everyone involved. Much research was done\nto try to discern how the nation will bounce back after this. Through\nour research we have determined that there will almost definitely be a\nsignificant upswing once we get back to operating normally.\n\n**Competition (Cellar Door) --** The Cellar Door has a lot more\ncompetition than Le Bistro. This means that we must work hard to show\nour guests what sets it apart. The unique environment as well as the\ngroup seating style will be points for us to differentiate ourselves. A\nnew focus on the kitchen and bar will help us give our guests the best\nproducts we can and aid in them choosing us over our competition\n\n**Small, Niche Market (Le Bistro) --** The fine dining market is a\nrelatively small market in our area. This means that we must compete\nover fewer guests. In efforts to combat this we will be continuing to\ndifferentiate ourselves moving forward. It is also our goal to feel more\naccessible to more people allowing us to grow our market.\n\n**Consumer Behavior (Cellar Door) --** The Cellar Door has been a tapas\nrestaurant since its inception. Our area has not been properly educated\non exactly what tapas is. Moving forward we will take the tapas part\naway from the brand. The Cellar Door will be focused solely on small\nplates instead of tapas. This will move it away from any Spanish\ninfluences and allow more exploration with the menu. There will also be\nfervent work done in the training of The Cellar Door servers to help\nthem craft a unique experience for their guests.\n\n# Operating Plan\n\n**Stage of Development**: ARI has been operating for 8 years under\nmultiple management teams. The current management team that is working\nto purchase the restaurants has already been working to improve\nefficiency and profitability. Large strides have been made in\ncontrolling costs and implementing new standards for employees. Special\nattention has been given to lowering food cost, controlling labor cost,\nand improving inventory management. While previously being understaffed\nsignificant improvements were made in fixing many of the areas that had\nbeen neglected. With proper staffing these numbers will continue to\nimprove and be able to be maintained. Daily operational plans cover all\nnecessary points of risk including but not limited to food safety\nstandards, server interactions with guests, sales analysis, and\ninventory management. Necessary lease hold improvements such as bar\nrenovations, floor replacement, painting, as well as, chair reupholstery\nand minor repairs will bring the dining room and kitchen areas up to\ndate.\n\n- ![](media/image16.emf){width=\"4.716666666666667in\"\n height=\"1.8138888888888889in\"}**Hours of Operation**\n\n![](media/image17.emf){width=\"3.5166666666666666in\"\nheight=\"1.698611111111111in\"}![](media/image17.emf){width=\"6.081944444444445in\"\nheight=\"1.6666666666666667in\"}**\\**\n\n- **Day-to-Day Operations:**\n\n - Purchasing and Receiving\n\n - All food orders will require a purchase order form to be completed\n by the Executive Chef or Kitchen Manager and presented to the VP\n of Food and Beverage:\n\n - Primary food order is generated once weekly based on inventory\n counts and par value system. Primary order must be submitted by\n Wednesday at 12:00 PM.\n\n - Supplemental food orders happen from our primary vendor once\n weekly and are generated from par value system and daily inventory\n items. Supplemental food orders must be submitted by Sunday at\n 12:00 PM.\n\n - Specialty food orders can be placed up to twice a week with\n approval from the COO. Specialty food orders will be submitted on\n a need basis at the discretion of the COO.\n\n - All alcoholic beverage orders will require a purchase order form\n to be completed by the Le Bistro and Cellar Door Assistant\n Managers and presented to the COO.\n\n - Deliveries will be received by a key employee designated by the\n immediate supervising Corporate Officer. Key employees will cross\n check quantity and quality of items received to the corresponding\n purchase order. Items received that do not meet company standards\n will be refused and returned with driver. Additionally, any\n discrepancies identified should be annotated and reported to key\n employees' immediate supervisor.\n\n - Preparation\n\n - All employees are required to complete opening checklist daily\n (Appendix p. 147-171).\n\n - Managers\n\n - Servers\n\n - Cooks\n\n - Par values will be set for all menu items based on projected\n sales and previous sales\n\n - Cooks are required to complete prep lists daily to fill all\n par values set for service\n\n - Cooks are to have stations set and stocked before service\n begins. Manager on duty will do a walkthrough before service\n to check par values and that proper setup has been completed\n\n - Service\n\n - Servers, steps of service (see server training manual Appendix p.\n 92-146)\n\n - Cooks during service are required to produce food in the manner\n learned during training\n\n - Cooks will focus on a few key points during service including:\n\n - Proper Food Handling (Following Servsafe Guidelines)\n\n - Proper Portioning\n\n - Proper Presentation\n\n - Quality Control\n\n - Timeliness\n\n - Station Cleanliness\n\n - Managers will monitor all work being done during service, aiding\n any staff member that needs help\n\n - Managers will be doing table touches throughout service to check\n and maintain guest satisfaction\n\n - Cleanup\n\n - All employees are required to complete closing checklists before\n clocking out for shift (Appendix p. 147-171).\n\n - Managers\n\n - Servers\n\n - Cooks\n\n - Managers will checkout subordinates at end of shift\n\n - Reporting\n\n - Daily reports will be collected and filed by the closing managers.\n Reports to be ran daily are:\n\n - Cash Reconciliation\n\n - Manager Log\n\n - Discounts, voids, and coupons\n\n - Incidents\n\n - Weekly reports will be collected and presented by the appropriate\n manager. Reports to be ran weekly are:\n\n - Sales Report\n\n - Cost of Goods Sold\n\n - Prime Cost Report\n\n - Cash Flow Report\n\n - Labor Report\n\n - Waste Report\n\n - Weekly Inventory\n\n - Monthly reports will be collected and presented by the appropriate\n manager. Reports to be ran monthly are:\n\n - A comprehensive report that includes aggregate amounts from\n respective weekly reports with additional reporting on\n year-over-year growth.\n\n - Profit loss statements\n\n - Projections\n\n- **Facilities:**\n\n - Le Bistro\n\n - Square Footage: 2,550 sq. ft.\n\n - Dining Room\n\n - Number of Seats: 64\n\n - Bar Seats: 10\n\n - Capacity During COVID-19: 37\n\n - Open Kitchen\n\n - Once a quarter all large equipment is inspected and receives\n preventative maintenance\n\n- **COVID-19 Operations:** Effective May 26^th^ these are the guidelines\n ARI will follow. While many are not mandatory, we feel them necessary\n to adequately keep our guests and employees safe. These practices are\n taking place at both Le Bistro and The Cellar Door.\n\n- **Social Distancing:**\n\n\n\n- **INDOOR SEATING CAPACITY**- ARI will limit its seating capacity to a\n maximum of 50% with all seated tables being at least 6 feet apart\n\n- **BAR**- Guests will not be allowed to gather at any bars, any guests\n who do not come together will be 6 feet apart at minimum\n\n- **WAITING AREAS**- In the case that more than one group will be\n waiting at a time we will not allow guests to congregate to wait in a\n shared space. Any guest that is waiting will be asked to wait in their\n car or outside and will be called when their table is ready\n\n\n\n- **Reducing Contact:**\n\n - **CLEAR PATHS-**Clear paths in and around the restaurants will be\n designated by signage in the restaurants\n\n - **LIMITED STAFF INTERACTION-** Wait staff will limit the number of\n times they visit a guest\n\n - **RESERVATIONS ENCOURAGED-** We will encourage reservations so that\n we can accurately separate guest visits to reduce contact with other\n guests\n\n - **MENUS-** Disposable and limited menus will be provided to all\n guests\n\n\n\n- **New Employee Protocols**\n\n - **EMPLOYEE SCREENING-** Employees will be screened to ensure that\n they have not been in contact with anyone that has any symptoms. We\n will also confirm that they aren't feeling symptoms. We would much\n rather operate with a smaller staff than risk endangering anyone\n\n - **EMPLOYEE TEMPERATURES-** Employees will be heavily encouraged to\n take their temperature before reporting into work. We will also\n purchase a no-contact thermometer to screen the employees\n\n - **SICK? STAY HOME! -** Any employees that show any sign of being\n sick will have to leave the premises immediately and should pursue\n testing for coronavirus, if they show signs, they should not show up\n to work in the first place\n\n - **TRAINING --** All employees will be trained on the importance of\n heightened cleanliness and to wash their hands more frequently,\n there will also be hand sanitizer provided to ensure their hands are\n always germ free\n\n - **FACE COVERINGS**- All employees will always be required to wear\n face coverings\n\n - **GLOVES**- All employees will always be required to wear gloves\n\n\n\n- **Cleaning Standards:**\n\n - **CLEANLINESS-** Much work has been done to sanitize and clean both\n Le Bistro and The Cellar Door, the management team spent a month\n working hard to ensure we could provide our guests with a safe and\n clean environment\n\n - **CLEANING SOLUTIONS-** The cleaning solutions used are approved by\n the EPA and sanitization has been done according to the CDC\n\n - **SANIZATION-** Every time a guest leaves the table and chairs will\n be thoroughly sanitized before another guest can sit there, all\n surfaces have been sanitized and all product has been removed from\n the restaurants\n\n - **CLEANING SCHEDULES-** Cleaning schedules more than doubled for all\n areas including the kitchen, dining rooms, restrooms and hallways\n\n\n\n- **Safety:**\n\n - **NO BUFFET-** No buffet or self-serve will be allowed, this is in\n accordance with the WV guidelines, we apologize to anyone this may\n inconvenience\n\n - **SIGNAGE-** Signage will be posted stating that anyone with any\n symptoms of coronavirus is not allowed on the premise\n\n - **CONTACTLESS CASHING OUT-** We will utilize our email receipt\n technology to keep the cashing out process to the least amount of\n contact possible, we will also be able to cash out guests without\n ever touching their card\n\n - **DISPOSABLES ENCOURAGED-** Bottles and cans will be encouraged for\n beverages\n\n - **DISH SAFETY-** Our dishwasher operates at such a high temperature\n and with disinfectants so we will be able to safely use glassware,\n silverware and plate ware. If any guest feels uncomfortable with\n this, we will have disposable options available.\n\n![](media/image19.png){width=\"10.022916666666667in\"\nheight=\"6.142361111111111in\"}**Organizational Chart:**\n\n**Management and Key Employees:**\n\n![](media/image20.png){width=\"10.341881014873142in\"\nheight=\"4.9372069116360455in\"}\n\n![](media/image21.png){width=\"10.114583333333334in\"\nheight=\"6.365581802274716in\"}\n\n**Management and Key Employees:** Abraham Restaurant Industries Inc.\nwill be headed by the founding member of Navi Inc. According to Nielsen's 2015 Global\nCorporate Sustainability Report, [66% of consumers would spend\nmore](http://www.nielsen.com/us/en/insights/reports/2015/the-sustainability-imperative.html) on\na product if it came from a sustainable brand. Up to 73% of the surveyed\nmillennials had a similar view. A study done by Statista in 2018 showed\nthe following: 20% of Americans think heavily about the sustainable\nproduction of their food, 59% of Americans are interested in sustainable\nseafood, 41% of Americans are very interested in sustainable meat. \nPrior to re-opening, we will also run a marketing campaign advertising\nnew ownership. The \"New Ownership Campaign\" will be vital to growth in\nguest count and sales.\n\n**Marketing Plan:**\n\n- **Media Advertising:**\n\n\n\n- *Newspaper (Pre-opening Only):*\n\n> Reach out to reporters/writers from Huntington's Herald Dispatch,\n> Marshall University's student newspaper The Parthenon, and Ashland's\n> The Daily Independent, informing them of the unique business venture\n> with change in ownership, renovation efforts, new offerings, and\n> re-open date. As a result of our positive relationship with Marshall\n> and The Herald Dispatch, this will be a no-cost marketing activity.\n\n- *Magazines*:\n\n> Contact industry specific and statewide magazines, such as WV Living,\n> New South Media, WV Executive, Taste! WV, West Virginia Hospitality &\n> Travel Association, Marshall Magazine, and WV Weddings to seek\n> coverage of the story about new ownership, renovations and updates,\n> and re-opening date.\n\n- *Television:*\n\n> Media Release: Prior to open, we will reach out to our contacts at\n> WSAZ and WCHS informing them of the change in ownership, renovation\n> efforts, new offerings, and re-open date. We will also invite them to\n> see the renovations and to dinner upon re-open. As a result of our\n> efforts in community involvement, reporters from both WSAZ and WCHS\n> often run stories/attend our events and invite us in for live\n> interviews. This will be a no-cost marketing activity.\n>\n> Commercials[:]{.underline}\n>\n> WCHS and WSAZ offer periodic specials in which we trade gift cards\n> (which they then sell for 50% off) for commercial airtime. We will\n> take advantage of the trade opportunities, as they reduce the\n> immediate impact on cashflow, allowing us to pay for the commercials\n> over time (as guests redeem the gift cards). Furthermore, our COGS\n> average is 33%, which increases the value of the airtime, as we\n> receive airtime valued at 50% of the gift cards traded.\n>\n> *Radio:*\n>\n> iHeart Media is our main radio advertising partner. Providing the experience diners want will\nresult in greater guest retention, increased foot traffic, higher server\nsales and much higher revenues. Proper execution is completely reliant\non a complete management team, proper staffing, and impeccable training.\nThe following highlights key sales areas and strategy aspects:\n\n- **In-House (Server Sales):** This objective will be the direct\n responsibility of the Chief Human Resources Officer and the Front of\n House Assistant Managers, with oversight and guidance by the CEO.\n Guest average consistently increased from 2016 (\\$28.11/guest) through\n 2018 (\\$31.71/guest), until 2019 (\\$30.72/guest) when it decreased by\n \\$1/guest. This decrease resulted in a minimum of \\$35,647 in lost\n revenue and was a direct result of under-staffing (in terms of both\n Management and hourly employees). Increased guest average will be\n achieved by:\n\n - On-going training with staff on up-sell techniques such as S.I.E\n (Suggest, Inform, Endorse)\n\n - On-going product knowledge training with staff through daily\n pre-shift meetings, and quarterly staff meeting/training sessions\n\n - Attractive presentation of up-sell items (Specialty Cocktails,\n Appetizers, Desserts)\n\n - Attractive Display areas at Le Bistro (Bar Renovation) for Wine,\n Beer and Desserts\n\n - Consistent execution of promotional marketing materials\n\n - \n\n \n\n - Table Tents\n\n - Menu Inserts\n\n - Limited Menu Specials\n\n - Posters\n\n - Signage\n\n - Phone Greets\n\n - TV Screens\n\n \n\n - \n\n - **Guest Count (Foot Traffic, Guest Retention):** This objective is\n reliant on the management team as a single unit, working together to\n ensure guests never experience a lapse in service or a subpar\n experience. The \"new ownership\" marketing campaign will be the\n driving force in early guest count increases; flawless execution\n during reopen will result in significant and sustainable guest\n retention. Daily guests then become our social media influencers,\n and word of mouth marketing will bring lost guests back to Le Bistro\n and The Cellar Door. In 2015, when Cellar Door opened for business,\n past management and current owners failed to realize the importance\n of management, subsequently costing ARI millions of dollars. From\n 2016-2019 the yearly guest count has fallen by more than 15,000;\n prior to the open of Cellar Door (2012-2014), Le Bistro had\n experienced 20%+ growth in guest count year over year. We will\n achieve guest retention, increased foot traffic, and ultimately a\n higher year-end guest count with the following strategy/practices:\n\n - Marketing campaign prior to open focused on unique business\n venture with new ownership, new management, renovations, and new\n offerings\n\n - Proper staffing and execution of re-opening\n\n - Training for both FOH and BOH team members 2 weeks prior to\n re-open, detailing higher service standards, new menu items, new\n management and staffing structure, etc.\n\n - Hire additional Servers and Bartenders in preparation for the\n projected increase in sales.\n\n - Hire chefs to properly staff all kitchen positions\n\n - New full-time FOH management positions will be highly engaged with\n guests through table touches and guest interaction, paying special\n attention to regulars, birthdays, anniversaries and other special\n occasions\n\n - Renovations and Updates\n\n - Le Bistro Bar - converting the main bar (4-5 seats) into a\n semi-private dining space for guests (6-8 seats) and moving the\n equipment to the Chef Bar (10 seats). This will create an\n aesthetically pleasing back drop when walking by the storefront,\n bring in more patrons that enjoy bar service, allow us to\n regularly staff a bartender, improve speed of service, and will\n drive excitement in our existing regulars to come see the new\n look.\n\n - Reupholstering the chairs in Le Bistro's dining room that are\n showing excess wear\n\n - Replace the broken chandelier\n\n - Optional improvements include adding mood lighting for dinner\n service at Le Bistro, painting the dining room at Le Bistro, and\n adding a door from Le Bistro leading to the elevators that take\n you to the Cellar Door (guests would no longer have to walk\n outside to get to Cellar Door and it would serve as cross\n promoting, encouraging guests to visit both locations during\n their visit)\n\n - Special Events at the Cellar Door\n\n - Events in partnership with local non-profits, such as Battle of\n the Bartenders with Huntington Pride, Sip and Savor with Faith\n in Action, Story Slams with Huntington Comedy, and Film Trivia\n with Marshall's Film Club\n\n - Events in partnership with other businesses such as Paint & Sip,\n Full Circle Gifts and Goods, and Forget Me Knots to offer a\n unique, catered workshop experience\n\n - Events in partnership with Marshall University Student Affairs\n and Marshall University Alumni during Week of Welcome,\n Homecoming, Commencement, Orientation, and Green and White Days\n\n - Quarterly Murder Mystery Dinner Events\n\n - Bi-Monthly Speakeasy Nights\n\n - Regular holiday and other themed events such as our famous New\n Year's Eve party\n\n - Frequent tap takeovers, wine and bourbon tastings, and other\n partnerships with breweries, distilleries, and wineries\n\n - Have all events consistently posted (on social media and\n websites) 3 months in advance, with active social media\n marketing beginning 3 to 5 weeks out depending on the event\n\n - Consistent on-going marketing initiatives that are frequently\n assessed, adjusted, and updated\n\n - Staying ahead of food and alcohol trends, as well as maintaining a\n focused commitment to picture-perfect presentation of all dishes\n and beverages\n\n - **Catering Sales:** Catering initiatives will be the direct\n responsibility of the Chief Experience Officer and the Special\n Events Coordinator. The opportunity for growth in catering sales is\n exponential in the underserved Huntington and surrounding area. With\n the expertise and guidance of Dakota Maddox, sales will double, if\n not triple by the end of 2021.\n\n - The new administrative assistant, FOH manager positions, Special\n Events Coordinator, and oversight by CXO ensures timely response\n to catering inquiries, which will eliminate the loss of catering\n sales to competitors as a result of delayed responses. Prospective\n customer calls and emails inquiring about catering services will\n be viewed as an opportunity to turn those prospects into\n customers.\n\n - Increase and develop a number of preferred vendor relationships\n with florists, photographers, bridal shops, event planners,\n venues, videographers, DJs, and live musicians\n\n - Implement outreach efforts, including sales calls, in-person\n networking campaign, product samples and menu drop-offs, and\n loyalty programs. The CXO and the Special Events Coordinator will\n focus on the following target markets:\n\n - Local Businesses: Lunch Caterings, Business Events, Board\n Meetings, Holiday Parties\n\n - Middle Schools and High Schools: Field-trip Packages for French\n and Spanish classes, offering authentic cuisine\n\n - Non-profit Organizations: Fundraising and philanthropy events,\n board and committee meetings, outreach and recruitment events\n\n - Local Groups/Clubs: Periodic meetings, special events\n\n - Update EZCater: Currently ordering from us through EZCater\n requires a minimum lead time of 1 day. The menu will be adjusted\n to require a 2-3-hour lead time, drastically increasing\n accessibility for day-time catering drop-off orders\n\n\n\n- Geo-Targeted Marketing: Geo-market to severely under-serviced markets\n such as Ironton, Ashland, Teays Valley, and Hurricane\n\n- Rewards / Incentive Program: Offer discounted room rentals, off-site\n fees, and gift card rebates for repeat catering customers\n\n - Increase and develop a number of preferred catering relationships we\n have with venues that can facilitate 150+ person events\n\n - Attend local and surrounding bridal and wedding expos\n\n - Host periodic tastings and open houses targeting brides, social\n event planners, and professional event planners\n\n - Promote venue buy-out options for Le Bistro and The Cellar Door.\n\n - Establish ongoing customer communications processes to keep in\n contact with potential and recurring catering clients to maintain\n relationships and pursue new ones, follow up phone calls after each\n catering order on and off site to address any unresolved issues,\n gather feedback, and discuss future business opportunities,\n handwritten thank you notes, happy anniversary/birthday messages on\n the clients appropriate dates,\n\n - Conduct incentivized surveys that ask specific questions about\n consultation and ordering process, quality of menu and services\n provided, and general feedback\n\n \n\n - **Innovation and Technology**: The restaurant industry has been\n shifting dramatically in terms of trends relating to to-go,\n delivery, local sourcing for food and alcohol, transparency and\n more. With the COVID-19 pandemic, it is even more important that we\n identify and execute additional sources of income. The following\n list includes new revenue streams and expansions on existing revenue\n streams that have been in the planning phase for 1-2 years.\n\n - The Chief Operating Officer will introduce Meal Kit and Meal Prep\n services.\n\n - The \\$2.2 billion meal kit industry will grow 25 to 30% by 2022\n according to industry experts.\n\n - 49% of adults said they would buy a meal kit from their favorite\n restaurant.\n\n - According to Nielsen, one in four Americans had tried a meal kit\n service as of March 2017. Neilsen's study also found that men of\n all ages are 40% more likely to purchase meal kits than women of\n the same age and that Millennials and Generation X is 321% more\n likely to buy them than older generations.
